     <p><b>Syracuse University</b>, commonly referred to as <b>Syracuse</b>, '<b>Cuse</b>, or <b>SU</b>,<sup id="cite_ref-Marrone.27s_Focus_is_on_the_.27Cuse_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Marrone.27s_Focus_is_on_the_.27Cuse-6"><span>[</span>6<span>]</span></a></sup> is a private research university located in <a href="/wiki/Syracuse,_New_York" title="Syracuse, New York">Syracuse</a>, <a href="/wiki/New_York" title="New York">New York</a>, United States. Its roots can be traced back to Genesee Wesleyan Seminary, founded by the <a href="/wiki/Methodist_Episcopal_Church" title="Methodist Episcopal Church">Methodist Episcopal Church</a> in 1832, which also later founded <a href="/wiki/Genesee_College" title="Genesee College">Genesee College</a>. Following several years of debate over relocating the college to Syracuse, the university was founded independent of the college in 1870. Since 1920, the university has identified itself as <a href="/wiki/Nonsectarian" title="Nonsectarian">nonsectarian</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-rankingsandreviews_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rankingsandreviews-7"><span>[</span>7<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-princetonreview_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-princetonreview-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-collegestats_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-collegestats-9"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-youniversitytv_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-youniversitytv-10"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-cappex_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cappex-11"><span>[</span>11<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Syracuse_University_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Syracuse_University-12"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup> although it maintains a relationship with <a href="/wiki/The_United_Methodist_Church" title="The United Methodist Church" class="mw-redirect">The United Methodist Church</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Bylaws_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bylaws-13"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Relatedness_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Relatedness-14"><span>[</span>14<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-William_Joseph_Whalen.C2.A0.E2.80.94_Hospitals_.26_Universities_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-William_Joseph_Whalen.C2.A0.E2.80.94_Hospitals_.26_Universities-15"><span>[</span>15<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-IAMSCU_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IAMSCU-16"><span>[</span>16<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-SU_.26_UMC_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SU_.26_UMC-17"><span>[</span>17<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The campus is located in the <a href="/wiki/University_Hill,_Syracuse" title="University Hill, Syracuse">University Hill</a> neighborhood of Syracuse, east and southeast of <a href="/wiki/Downtown_Syracuse" title="Downtown Syracuse">downtown</a>, on one of the larger hills. Its large campus features an eclectic mix of buildings, ranging from nineteenth-century <a href="/wiki/Romanesque_architecture" title="Romanesque architecture">Romanesque</a> structures to contemporary buildings. SU is organized into 13 schools and colleges, with nationally recognized programs in <a href="/wiki/Syracuse_University_School_of_Information_Studies" title="Syracuse University School of Information Studies">information studies and library science</a>, <a href="/wiki/Syracuse_University_School_of_Architecture" title="Syracuse University School of Architecture">architecture</a>, <a href="/wiki/S._I._Newhouse_School_of_Public_Communications" title="S. I. Newhouse School of Public Communications">communications</a>, <a href="/wiki/Business_administration" title="Business administration">business administration</a>, <a href="/wiki/Public_administration" title="Public administration">public administration</a>, <a href="/wiki/Engineering" title="Engineering">engineering</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Syracuse_University_College_of_Arts_and_Sciences" title="Syracuse University College of Arts and Sciences">College of Arts and Sciences</a>.</p> 
     <p>Syracuse University athletic teams, known as the <a href="/wiki/Syracuse_Orange" title="Syracuse Orange">Orange</a>, participate in 20 intercollegiate sports. SU is a member of the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Coast_Conference" title="Atlantic Coast Conference">Atlantic Coast Conference</a> for all <a href="/wiki/NCAA" title="NCAA" class="mw-redirect">NCAA</a> <a href="/wiki/Division_I_(NCAA)" title="Division I (NCAA)">Division I</a> athletics, except for women's <a href="/wiki/Ice_hockey" title="Ice hockey">ice hockey</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/College_rowing_(United_States)" title="College rowing (United States)">rowing team</a>. SU is also a member of the <a href="/wiki/Eastern_College_Athletic_Conference" title="Eastern College Athletic Conference">Eastern College Athletic Conference</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Eastern_College_Athletic_Conference_.28ECAC.29_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Eastern_College_Athletic_Conference_.28ECAC.29-18"><span>[</span>18<span>]</span></a></sup></p>

     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Syracuse_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Founding">Founding</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Syracuse_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Founding">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>The <a href="/wiki/Genesee_Wesleyan_Seminary" title="Genesee Wesleyan Seminary">Genesee Wesleyan Seminary</a> was founded in 1832 by the Genesee <a href="/wiki/Annual_Conference" title="Annual Conference" class="mw-redirect">Annual Conference</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Methodist_Episcopal_Church" title="Methodist Episcopal Church">Methodist Episcopal Church</a> in Lima, New York, south of <a href="/wiki/Rochester,_New_York" title="Rochester, New York">Rochester</a>. In 1850, it was resolved to enlarge the institution from a seminary into a college, or to connect a college with the seminary, becoming <a href="/wiki/Genesee_College" title="Genesee College">Genesee College</a>. However, the location was soon thought by many to be insufficiently central. Its difficulties were compounded by the next set of technological changes: the railroad that displaced the Erie Canal as the region's economic engine bypassed Lima completely. The trustees of the struggling college then decided to seek a locale whose economic and transportation advantages could provide a better base of support.</p> 
     <div class="thumb tleft"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Henry_Jarvis_Raymond.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Henry_Jarvis_Raymond.jpg/180px-Henry_Jarvis_Raymond.jpg" width="180" height="226" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Henry_Jarvis_Raymond.jpg/270px-Henry_Jarvis_Raymond.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Henry_Jarvis_Raymond.jpg/360px-Henry_Jarvis_Raymond.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Henry_Jarvis_Raymond.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> A graduate of the Genesee Seminary, Henry Jarvis Raymond later went on to found the 
        <a href="/wiki/New_York_Times" title="New York Times" class="mw-redirect">New York Times</a>.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>The college began looking for a new home at the same time that Syracuse, ninety miles to the east, was engaged in a search to bring a university to the city, having failed to convince <a href="/wiki/Ezra_Cornell" title="Ezra Cornell">Ezra Cornell</a> and <a href="/wiki/Andrew_Dickson_White" title="Andrew Dickson White">Andrew Dickson White</a> to locate <a href="/wiki/Cornell_University" title="Cornell University">Cornell University</a> there rather than in <a href="/wiki/Ithaca,_New_York" title="Ithaca, New York">Ithaca</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-PioneerYears_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PioneerYears-19"><span>[</span>19<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Greene_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Greene-20"><span>[</span>20<span>]</span></a></sup> White pressed that the university should locate on the hill in <a href="/wiki/Syracuse,_New_York" title="Syracuse, New York">Syracuse</a> (the current location of Syracuse University) due to the city's attractive transportation hub, which would ease the recruitment of faculty, students, and other persons of note. However, as a young carpenter working in Syracuse, Cornell had been twice robbed of his wages,<sup id="cite_ref-reminiscences_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-reminiscences-21"><span>[</span>21<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-university_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-university-22"><span>[</span>22<span>]</span></a></sup> and thereafter considered Syracuse a <a href="/wiki/Sodom_and_Gomorrah" title="Sodom and Gomorrah">Sodom and Gomorrah</a> insisting that the university be located in <a href="/wiki/Ithaca,_New_York" title="Ithaca, New York">Ithaca</a> on his large farm on East Hill, overlooking the town and <a href="/wiki/Cayuga_Lake" title="Cayuga Lake">Cayuga Lake</a>. Meanwhile, there were several years of dispute between the Methodist ministers, Lima, and contending cities across the state, over proposals to move Genesee College to Syracuse. At the time, the ministers wanted a share of the funds from the <a href="/wiki/Morrill_Land_Grant_Act" title="Morrill Land Grant Act" class="mw-redirect">Morrill Land Grant Act</a> for Genesee College. Eventually, they agreed to a quid-pro quo donation of $25,000 from Ezra Cornell in exchange for their support for his bill. Cornell insisted the bargain be written into the bill and Cornell became New York State's Land Grant University in 1865. In 1869, Genesee College obtained New York State approval to move to Syracuse, but Lima got a court injunction to block the move, and Genesee stayed in Lima until it was dissolved in 1875.<sup id="cite_ref-found_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-found-23"><span>[</span>23<span>]</span></a></sup> At its founding on March 24, 1870, the state of New York granted Syracuse University its charter independent of Genesee College.<sup id="cite_ref-found_23-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-found-23"><span>[</span>23<span>]</span></a></sup> The City of Syracuse offered $100,000 to establish the school.<sup id="cite_ref-found_23-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-found-23"><span>[</span>23<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Jesse_T._Peck" title="Jesse T. Peck" class="mw-redirect">Bishop Jesse Truesdell Peck</a> donated $25,000 to the proposed school<sup id="cite_ref-dickinson_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dickinson-24"><span>[</span>24<span>]</span></a></sup> and was elected the first president of the Board of Trustees.<sup id="cite_ref-Greene_20-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Greene-20"><span>[</span>20<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Rev. Daniel Steele, a former Genesee College president, served as the first administrative leader of Syracuse until its Chancellor was appointed.<sup id="cite_ref-The_Hill:_an_illustrated_biography_of_Syracuse_University.2C_1870.E2.80.93present_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Hill:_an_illustrated_biography_of_Syracuse_University.2C_1870.E2.80.93present-25"><span>[</span>25<span>]</span></a></sup> The university opened in September 1871 in rented space downtown.<sup id="cite_ref-found_23-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-found-23"><span>[</span>23<span>]</span></a></sup> George F. Comstock, a member of the new University's Board of Trustees, had offered the school 50 acres (200,000&nbsp;m<sup>2</sup>) of farmland on a hillside to the southeast of the city center. Comstock intended Syracuse University and the hill to develop as an integrated whole; a contemporary account described the latter as &quot;a beautiful town ... springing up on the hillside and a community of refined and cultivated membership ... established near the spot which will soon be the center of a great and beneficent educational institution.&quot;<sup id="cite_ref-architectural_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-architectural-26"><span>[</span>26<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:352px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Annual_Class_of_Syracuse_University,_July_1876,_from_Robert_N._Dennis_collection_of_stereoscopic_views.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Annual_Class_of_Syracuse_University%2C_July_1876%2C_from_Robert_N._Dennis_collection_of_stereoscopic_views.jpg/350px-Annual_Class_of_Syracuse_University%2C_July_1876%2C_from_Robert_N._Dennis_collection_of_stereoscopic_views.jpg" width="350" height="177" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Annual_Class_of_Syracuse_University%2C_July_1876%2C_from_Robert_N._Dennis_collection_of_stereoscopic_views.jpg/525px-Annual_Class_of_Syracuse_University%2C_July_1876%2C_from_Robert_N._Dennis_collection_of_stereoscopic_views.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Annual_Class_of_Syracuse_University%2C_July_1876%2C_from_Robert_N._Dennis_collection_of_stereoscopic_views.jpg/700px-Annual_Class_of_Syracuse_University%2C_July_1876%2C_from_Robert_N._Dennis_collection_of_stereoscopic_views.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Annual_Class_of_Syracuse_University,_July_1876,_from_Robert_N._Dennis_collection_of_stereoscopic_views.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> First Annual Class of Syracuse University.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>The university was founded as coeducational, and President Peck stated at the opening ceremonies, &quot;The conditions of admission shall be equal to all persons... there shall be no invidious discrimination here against woman.... brains and heart shall have a fair chance... &quot;<sup id="cite_ref-coed_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-coed-27"><span>[</span>27<span>]</span></a></sup> Syracuse implemented this policy with a high proportion of women students. The ratio between male and female students during the 19th century in the College of Liberal Arts was approximately even. The College of Fine Arts was predominantly female, and a low ratio of women enrolled as students in the College of Medicine and the College of Law.<sup id="cite_ref-coed_27-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-coed-27"><span>[</span>27<span>]</span></a></sup> Men and women were taught together in the same courses, and many extra-curricular activities were coeducational as well. Syracuse also developed &quot;women-only&quot; organizations, such as the Ladies' Glee Club, the Y.W.C.A. and various sororities.<sup id="cite_ref-coed_27-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-coed-27"><span>[</span>27<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Expansion">Expansion</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Syracuse_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Expansion">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>Coeducation at Syracuse traced its roots to the early days of the Genesee College where suffragists like <a href="/wiki/Frances_Willard_(suffragist)" title="Frances Willard (suffragist)">Frances Willard</a> and <a href="/wiki/Belva_Lockwood" title="Belva Lockwood" class="mw-redirect">Belva Lockwood</a> began to distinguish themselves nationally. However, the progressive &quot;co-ed&quot; policies initiated at Genesee would soon find controversy at the new university in Syracuse.<sup id="cite_ref-Greene_20-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Greene-20"><span>[</span>20<span>]</span></a></sup> Colleges and universities admitted few women students in the 1870s. Administrators and faculty argued women had inferior minds and could not master mathematics and the classics. Dr. <a href="/wiki/Erastus_Otis_Haven" title="Erastus Otis Haven">Erastus Otis Haven</a>, Syracuse University chancellor and former president of the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Michigan" title="University of Michigan">University of Michigan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Northwestern_University" title="Northwestern University">Northwestern University</a>, maintained that women should receive the advantages of higher education. He enrolled his daughter, Frances, at SU, where she was initiated in the newly formed Gamma Phi Beta sorority.<sup id="cite_ref-Greene_20-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Greene-20"><span>[</span>20<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <div class="thumb tleft"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:HendricksChapel.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/HendricksChapel.jpg/200px-HendricksChapel.jpg" width="200" height="153" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/HendricksChapel.jpg/300px-HendricksChapel.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/HendricksChapel.jpg/400px-HendricksChapel.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:HendricksChapel.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> Hendricks Chapel
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>In the late 1880s the University resumed construction on the south side of University Place. Holden Observatory (1887) was followed by two Romanesque Revival buildings&nbsp;– von Ranke Library (1889), now Tolley Administration Building, and Crouse College (1889). Together with the Hall of Languages, these first buildings formed the basis for the &quot;Old Row,&quot; a grouping which, along with its companion Lawn, established one of Syracuse's most enduring images.<sup id="cite_ref-architectural_26-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-architectural-26"><span>[</span>26<span>]</span></a></sup> The emphatically linear organization of these buildings along the brow of the hill follows a tradition of American campus planning which dates to the construction of the &quot;Yale Row&quot; in the 1790s. At Syracuse, the Old Row continued to provide the framework for growth well into the twentieth century.<sup id="cite_ref-architectural_26-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-architectural-26"><span>[</span>26<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>From its founding until through early 1920s, the University grew rapidly. It offered programs in the physical sciences and modern languages, and in 1873, Syracuse added one of the first architecture programs in the U.S.<sup id="cite_ref-Greene2_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Greene2-28"><span>[</span>28<span>]</span></a></sup> In 1874, Syracuse created the nation's first bachelor of fine arts degree,<sup id="cite_ref-Syracuse_University_History_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Syracuse_University_History-29"><span>[</span>29<span>]</span></a></sup> and in 1876, the school offered its first post-graduate courses in the College of Arts and Sciences.<sup id="cite_ref-Greene2_28-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Greene2-28"><span>[</span>28<span>]</span></a></sup> SU created its first doctoral program in 1911.<sup id="cite_ref-SU1906_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SU1906-30"><span>[</span>30<span>]</span></a></sup> SU's school of journalism, now the <a href="/wiki/S.I._Newhouse_School_of_Public_Communications" title="S.I. Newhouse School of Public Communications" class="mw-redirect">S.I. Newhouse School of Public Communications</a>, was established at Syracuse in 1934.<sup id="cite_ref-SU1931_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SU1931-31"><span>[</span>31<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The growth of Syracuse University from a small liberal arts college into a major comprehensive university were due to the efforts of two men, Chancellor <a href="/wiki/James_Roscoe_Day" title="James Roscoe Day">James Day</a> and <a href="/wiki/John_Dustin_Archbold" title="John Dustin Archbold">John Archbold</a>. James Roscoe Day was serving the Calvary Church in New York City where he befriended Archbold. Together, the two dynamic figures would oversee the first of two great periods of campus renewal in Syracuse's history.<sup id="cite_ref-Greene_20-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Greene-20"><span>[</span>20<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>John Dustin Archbold was a capitalist, philanthropist, and President of the Board of Trustees at Syracuse University. He was known as John D. Rockefeller’s right hand man and successor at the <a href="/wiki/Standard_Oil" title="Standard Oil">Standard Oil</a> Company. He was a close friend of Syracuse University Chancellor James R. Day, and gave almost $6&nbsp;million to the University over his lifetime.<sup id="cite_ref-Greene_20-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Greene-20"><span>[</span>20<span>]</span></a></sup> Said a journalist in 1917:</p> 
     <blockquote> 
      <p>Mr. Archbold’s ... is the president of the board of trustees of Syracuse University, an institution which has prospered so remarkably since his connection with it that its student roll has increased from hundreds to over 4,000, including 1,500 young women, placing it in the ranks of the foremost institutions of learning in the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-Men_who_are_making_America_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Men_who_are_making_America-32"><span>[</span>32<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     </blockquote> 
     <p>In addition to keeping the university financially solvent during its early years, he also contributed funds for eight buildings, including the full cost of Archbold Stadium (opened 1907, demolished 1978), Sims Hall (men's dormitory, 1907), the Archbold Gymnasium (1909, nearly destroyed by fire in 1947, but still in use), and the oval athletic field.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Modern">Modern</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Syracuse_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Modern">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>After <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>, Syracuse University began to transform into a major research institution. Enrollment increased in the four years after the war due to the <a href="/wiki/G.I._Bill" title="G.I. Bill">G.I. Bill</a>, which paid tuition, room, board, and a small allowance for veterans returning from World War II. In 1946, SU admitted 9,464 freshmen, nearly four times greater than the previous incoming class.<sup id="cite_ref-SU1931_31-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SU1931-31"><span>[</span>31<span>]</span></a></sup> Branch campuses were established in <a href="/wiki/Endicott,_New_York" title="Endicott, New York">Endicott, New York</a> and <a href="/wiki/Utica,_New_York" title="Utica, New York">Utica, New York</a>.</p> 
     <blockquote> 
      <p>The velocity with which the university sped through its change into a major research institution was astounding. By the end of the 1950s, Syracuse ranked twelfth nationally in terms of the amount of its sponsored research, and it had over four hundred professors and graduate students engaging in that investigation.<sup id="cite_ref-Greene2_28-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Greene2-28"><span>[</span>28<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     </blockquote> 
     <p>From the early 1950s through the 1960s, Syracuse University added programs and staff that continued the transformation of the school into a research university. In 1954, Arthur Phillips was recruited from <a href="/wiki/Massachusetts_Institute_of_Technology" title="Massachusetts Institute of Technology">MIT</a> and started the first <a href="/wiki/Pathogen" title="Pathogen">pathogen</a>-free animal research laboratory. The lab focused on studying medical problems using animal models. The School of Social Work, which eventually merged into the College of Human Ecology, was founded in 1956.<sup id="cite_ref-Syracuse_University_History.2C_1951.E2.80.931960_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Syracuse_University_History.2C_1951.E2.80.931960-33"><span>[</span>33<span>]</span></a></sup> Syracuse's College of Engineering also founded the nation's second oldest computer engineering and bioengineering programs. In 1962, <a href="/wiki/Samuel_Irving_Newhouse,_Sr." title="Samuel Irving Newhouse, Sr.">Samuel Irving Newhouse, Sr.</a> donated $15&nbsp;million to begin construction of a school of communications, eventually known as the <a href="/wiki/SI_Newhouse_School_of_Public_Communications" title="SI Newhouse School of Public Communications" class="mw-redirect">SI Newhouse School of Public Communications</a>. In 1966, Syracuse University was admitted to the <a href="/wiki/Association_of_American_Universities" title="Association of American Universities">Association of American Universities</a>, an <a href="/wiki/Organization" title="Organization">organization</a> of leading research <a href="/wiki/University" title="University">universities</a> devoted to maintaining a strong system of academic <a href="/wiki/Research" title="Research">research</a> and education.<sup id="cite_ref-Syracuse_University_History.2C_1961.E2.80.931970_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Syracuse_University_History.2C_1961.E2.80.931970-34"><span>[</span>34<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <table class="wikitable" style="font-size:90%; width:100%; border:0; text-align:center; line-height:120%;">

     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Pan_Am_Flight_103">Pan Am Flight 103</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Syracuse_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Pan Am Flight 103">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Syracuse_University_Flight_103_Memorial.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Syracuse_University_Flight_103_Memorial.jpg/200px-Syracuse_University_Flight_103_Memorial.jpg" width="200" height="150" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Syracuse_University_Flight_103_Memorial.jpg/300px-Syracuse_University_Flight_103_Memorial.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Syracuse_University_Flight_103_Memorial.jpg/400px-Syracuse_University_Flight_103_Memorial.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Syracuse_University_Flight_103_Memorial.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> SU's Flight 103 Memorial
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/Pan_Am_Flight_103" title="Pan Am Flight 103">Pan Am Flight 103</a>
     </div> 
     <p>On December 21, 1988, 35 Syracuse University students were killed in the terrorist bombing of <a href="/wiki/Pan_Am_Flight_103" title="Pan Am Flight 103">Pan Am Flight 103</a> over <a href="/wiki/Lockerbie,_Scotland" title="Lockerbie, Scotland" class="mw-redirect">Lockerbie</a>, <a href="/wiki/Scotland" title="Scotland">Scotland</a>. The students were returning from a study-abroad program in Europe.</p> 
     <p>That evening, Syracuse University went on with a <a href="/wiki/Basketball" title="Basketball">basketball</a> game just hours after the attack, for which it was severely criticized.<sup id="cite_ref-Conduct_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Conduct-35"><span>[</span>35<span>]</span></a></sup> The conduct of university officials in making the decision was also brought to the attention of the NCAA.<sup id="cite_ref-Conduct_35-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Conduct-35"><span>[</span>35<span>]</span></a></sup> The day after the bombing, the university's chancellor, <a href="/wiki/Melvin_A._Eggers" title="Melvin A. Eggers">Melvin A. Eggers</a>, said on nationwide television that he should have cancelled the event.<sup id="cite_ref-Conduct_35-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Conduct-35"><span>[</span>35<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-A_Tragic_End_to_the_Semester_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-A_Tragic_End_to_the_Semester-36"><span>[</span>36<span>]</span></a></sup> After the <a href="/wiki/September_11_attacks" title="September 11 attacks">attacks on September 11, 2001</a>, the NCAA ordered <i>all</i> football games scheduled for the weekend after the attacks canceled so that schools do not make the same mistake Syracuse University did after Pan Am Flight 103.<sup id="cite_ref-Many_Sporting_Events_Called_Off_or_Postponed_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Many_Sporting_Events_Called_Off_or_Postponed-37"><span>[</span>37<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Pan_Am_Horror_Recalled_On_the_Night_270_People_Died.2C_SU_Played_On_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Pan_Am_Horror_Recalled_On_the_Night_270_People_Died.2C_SU_Played_On-38"><span>[</span>38<span>]</span></a></sup> (the bombing of Flight 103 was the deadliest terrorist attack against the United States prior to the attacks on September 11, 2001.<sup id="cite_ref-An_Act_of_War.3F.E2.80.93On_the_15th_Anniversary_a_Former_Pilot_Compares_the_Downing_of_Pan_Am_103_to_the_Sept._11.2C_2001_Attacks_on_America_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-An_Act_of_War.3F.E2.80.93On_the_15th_Anniversary_a_Former_Pilot_Compares_the_Downing_of_Pan_Am_103_to_the_Sept._11.2C_2001_Attacks_on_America-39"><span>[</span>39<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-20_years_later.2C_pain_of_Lockerbie_still_fresh_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20_years_later.2C_pain_of_Lockerbie_still_fresh-40"><span>[</span>40<span>]</span></a></sup>)</p> 
     <p>In April 1990, Syracuse University dedicated a memorial wall to the students killed on Flight 103, constructed at the entrance to the main campus in front of the Hall of Languages. Every year the university holds &quot;Remembrance Week&quot; during the fall semester to commemorate the students. On December 21 a service in the university's chapel at 2:03&nbsp;p.m. (19:03&nbsp;<a href="/wiki/UTC" title="UTC" class="mw-redirect">UTC</a>) marks the exact minute on that date in 1988 when the plane exploded. The University also maintains a link to the tragedy with the &quot;Remembrance Scholars&quot; program, when 35 senior students receive scholarships during their final year at the University. With the &quot;Lockerbie Scholars&quot; program, two graduating students from Lockerbie Academy study at Syracuse for one year.<sup id="cite_ref-Lockerbie_Scholars_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lockerbie_Scholars-41"><span>[</span>41<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Campus">Campus</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Syracuse_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Campus">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Syracuse_University_HallofLanguages.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/Syracuse_University_HallofLanguages.jpg/200px-Syracuse_University_HallofLanguages.jpg" width="200" height="134" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/Syracuse_University_HallofLanguages.jpg/300px-Syracuse_University_HallofLanguages.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/Syracuse_University_HallofLanguages.jpg/400px-Syracuse_University_HallofLanguages.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Syracuse_University_HallofLanguages.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> Hall of Languages
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Hendrickschapelsu.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Hendrickschapelsu.jpg/200px-Hendrickschapelsu.jpg" width="200" height="150" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Hendrickschapelsu.jpg/300px-Hendrickschapelsu.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Hendrickschapelsu.jpg/400px-Hendrickschapelsu.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Hendrickschapelsu.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> Hendricks Chapel
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>The university is set on a campus that features an eclectic mix of buildings, ranging from nineteenth-century <a href="/wiki/Romanesque_architecture" title="Romanesque architecture">Romanesque</a> structures to contemporary buildings designed by renowned architects such as <a href="/wiki/I.M._Pei" title="I.M. Pei" class="mw-redirect">I.M. Pei</a>. The center of campus, with its grass quadrangle, landscaped walkways, and outdoor sculptures, offers students the amenities of a traditional college experience. The university overlooks <a href="/wiki/Downtown_Syracuse" title="Downtown Syracuse">downtown Syracuse</a>, a medium-sized city (140,600 residents in 2008).<sup id="cite_ref-Best_Places_to_Live-Syracuse.2C_NY_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Best_Places_to_Live-Syracuse.2C_NY-42"><span>[</span>42<span>]</span></a></sup> The school also owns a <a href="/wiki/Sheraton_Hotel" title="Sheraton Hotel" class="mw-redirect">Sheraton Hotel</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-S.U._Acquires_Sheraton_Hotel_43-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-S.U._Acquires_Sheraton_Hotel-43"><span>[</span>43<span>]</span></a></sup> Drumlins Country Club—a nearby <a href="/wiki/Golf_course" title="Golf course">golf course</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Drumlins_Country_Club._Syracuse.2C_New_York._44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Drumlins_Country_Club._Syracuse.2C_New_York.-44"><span>[</span>44<span>]</span></a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Lubin" title="Joseph Lubin">Joseph I. Lubin</a> House in <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">New York City</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Lubin_House:_Welcome_45-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lubin_House:_Welcome-45"><span>[</span>45<span>]</span></a></sup> the Paul Greenberg House in <a href="/wiki/Washington,_D.C." title="Washington, D.C.">Washington, D.C.</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Syracuse_University_Greenberg_House_46-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Syracuse_University_Greenberg_House-46"><span>[</span>46<span>]</span></a></sup> and the Minnowbrook Conference Center, a 30 acre (121,000 m&sup2;) retreat in the <a href="/wiki/Adirondack_mountains" title="Adirondack mountains" class="mw-redirect">Adirondack Mountains</a> of <a href="/wiki/Upstate_New_York" title="Upstate New York">Upstate New York</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Minnowbrook_Conference_Center_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Minnowbrook_Conference_Center-47"><span>[</span>47<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Pi_Chapter_House_of_Psi_Upsilon_Fraternity_1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Pi_Chapter_House_of_Psi_Upsilon_Fraternity_1.jpg/200px-Pi_Chapter_House_of_Psi_Upsilon_Fraternity_1.jpg" width="200" height="208" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Pi_Chapter_House_of_Psi_Upsilon_Fraternity_1.jpg/300px-Pi_Chapter_House_of_Psi_Upsilon_Fraternity_1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Pi_Chapter_House_of_Psi_Upsilon_Fraternity_1.jpg/400px-Pi_Chapter_House_of_Psi_Upsilon_Fraternity_1.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Pi_Chapter_House_of_Psi_Upsilon_Fraternity_1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> Pi Chapter House of Psi Upsilon Fraternity
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Main_campus">Main campus</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Syracuse_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Main campus">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>Also called &quot;North Campus,&quot; the Main Campus contains nearly all academic buildings and residence halls. Its centerpiece is The Kenneth A. Shaw Quadrangle, more affectionately known as &quot;The Quad&quot;, which is surrounded by academic and administrative buildings. The North Campus represents a large portion of the <a href="/wiki/University_Hill,_Syracuse" title="University Hill, Syracuse">University Hill</a> neighborhood. Buses run to South Campus, as well as <a href="/wiki/Downtown_Syracuse" title="Downtown Syracuse">downtown Syracuse</a> and other locations in the city.<sup id="cite_ref-Syracuse_University_Map_48-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Syracuse_University_Map-48"><span>[</span>48<span>]</span></a></sup> About 70 percent of students live in University housing. First- and second-year students are required to live on campus. All 22 residence halls are coeducational and each contain a lounge, laundry facility, and various social/study spaces. Residence halls are secured with a card access system. Residence halls are located on both Main Campus and South Campus, the latter of which is a five-minute ride via bus. Learning communities and interest housing options are also available. Food facilities include six residential dining centers, two food courts, and several cafes.</p> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Crousecollegesu.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/Crousecollegesu.jpg/200px-Crousecollegesu.jpg" width="200" height="200" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/Crousecollegesu.jpg/300px-Crousecollegesu.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/Crousecollegesu.jpg/400px-Crousecollegesu.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Crousecollegesu.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> Crouse College, the home of the school of music.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>The <a href="/wiki/Comstock_Tract_Buildings" title="Comstock Tract Buildings" class="mw-redirect">Comstock Tract Buildings</a>, a historic district of older buildings on the campus, was listed on the <a href="/wiki/National_Register_of_Historic_Places" title="National Register of Historic Places">National Register of Historic Places</a> in 1980.<sup id="cite_ref-nrhptextComstock_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nrhptextComstock-49"><span>[</span>49<span>]</span></a></sup> Three buildings on campus—the <a href="/wiki/Crouse_College,_Syracuse_University" title="Crouse College, Syracuse University">Crouse Memorial College</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Hall_of_Languages,_Syracuse_University" title="Hall of Languages, Syracuse University">Hall of Languages</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Pi_Chapter_House_of_Psi_Upsilon_Fraternity" title="Pi Chapter House of Psi Upsilon Fraternity">Pi Chapter House of Psi Upsilon Fraternity</a>—are individually listed on the National Register.<sup id="cite_ref-nris_50-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nris-50"><span>[</span>50<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>A few blocks walk from Main Campus on East Genesee St, the <a href="/wiki/Syracuse_Stage" title="Syracuse Stage">Syracuse Stage</a> building includes two <a href="/wiki/Proscenium" title="Proscenium">proscenium</a> theatres. The Storch is used primarily by the Drama Department and the Archbold is used primarily by Syracuse Stage, a professional <a href="/wiki/Regional_theater_in_the_United_States" title="Regional theater in the United States">regional theatre</a>.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="South_campus">South campus</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Syracuse_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: South campus">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>After World War II, a large, undeveloped hill owned by the university was used to house returning <a href="/wiki/Veterans" title="Veterans" class="mw-redirect">veterans</a> in military-style campus housing. During the 1970s, this housing was replaced by permanent two-level townhouses for two or three students each, or for graduate family housing. There are also three small residence halls which feature open doubles. South Campus is also home to the Institute for Sensory Research, Tennity Ice Pavilion, Goldstein Student Center, Skytop Office Building and 621 Skytop Road (for administration), and the InnComplete Pub, a graduate student bar. Just north is the headquarters of SU Athletics located in the Manley Athletics Complex. Approximately 2,500 students live on the South Campus, which is connected to the main campus by frequent bus service.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Downtown">Downtown</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Syracuse_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Downtown">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Su_Warehouse.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/Su_Warehouse.jpg/200px-Su_Warehouse.jpg" width="200" height="150" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/Su_Warehouse.jpg/300px-Su_Warehouse.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/Su_Warehouse.jpg/400px-Su_Warehouse.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Su_Warehouse.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> The Warehouse upon completion
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>In December 2004, the university announced that it had purchased or leased twelve buildings in <a href="/wiki/Downtown_Syracuse" title="Downtown Syracuse">downtown Syracuse</a>. Five Design Programs; Communication, Advertising, Interiors, Industrial, and Fashion; reside permanently in the newly renovated facilities, fittingly called <a href="/wiki/The_Warehouse_(Syracuse)" title="The Warehouse (Syracuse)">The Warehouse</a>, which was renovated by <a href="/wiki/Gluckman_Mayner_Architects" title="Gluckman Mayner Architects">Gluckman Mayner Architects</a>. Both programs were chosen to be located in the downtown area because of their history of working on projects directly with the community. The Warehouse also houses a contemporary art space that commissions, exhibits, and promotes the work of local and international artists in a variety of media. Hundreds of students and faculty have also been affected by the temporary move of the School of Architecture downtown for the $12&nbsp;million renovation of its campus facility, Slocum Hall.</p> 
     <p>Since 2009, the Syracuse Center of Excellence in Environmental and Energy Systems, led by Syracuse University in partnership with <a href="/wiki/Clarkson_University" title="Clarkson University">Clarkson University</a> and the <a href="/wiki/State_University_of_New_York_College_of_Environmental_Science_and_Forestry" title="State University of New York College of Environmental Science and Forestry">College Environmental Science and Forestry</a>, creates innovations in environmental and energy technologies that improve human health and productivity, security, and sustainability in urban and built environments.<sup id="cite_ref-Syracuse_Center_of_Excellence_in_Environmental_and_Energy_Innovations_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Syracuse_Center_of_Excellence_in_Environmental_and_Energy_Innovations-51"><span>[</span>51<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Excellence_in_Environmental_and_Energy_Innovations_52-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Excellence_in_Environmental_and_Energy_Innovations-52"><span>[</span>52<span>]</span></a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Department_of_African_American_Studies_-_Syracuse_University#Paul_Robeson_Performing_Arts_Company_.28PRPAC.29" title="Department of African American Studies - Syracuse University" class="mw-redirect">Paul Robeson Performing Arts Company</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Department_of_African_American_Studies_-_Syracuse_University#Community_Folk_Art_Center_.28CFAC.29" title="Department of African American Studies - Syracuse University" class="mw-redirect">Community Folk Art Center</a> will also be located downtown. On March 31, 2006, the university and the city announced an initiative to connect the main campus of the university with the arts and culture areas of downtown Syracuse and The Warehouse.<sup id="cite_ref-Welcome_to_Syracuse_University_News_53-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Welcome_to_Syracuse_University_News-53"><span>[</span>53<span>]</span></a></sup> At a new green data center, a natural gas-fueled on-site electrical co-generation system generates 100 percent of the center’s electricity while helping cool a couple of buildings.<sup id="cite_ref-go-green_54-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-go-green-54"><span>[</span>54<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The Connective Corridor project, supported by of public and private funds, will be a strip of cultural development that will connect the main campus of the university to downtown Syracuse, NY. In 2008, an <a href="/wiki/Civil_engineering" title="Civil engineering">engineering</a> firm is studying traffic patterns and lighting to commence the project. A design competition was held to determine the best design for the project.<sup id="cite_ref-The_Connective_Corridor.E2.80.94Project_Overview_55-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Connective_Corridor.E2.80.94Project_Overview-55"><span>[</span>55<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Metropolitan_Satellite_Locations">Metropolitan Satellite Locations</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Syracuse_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Metropolitan Satellite Locations">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>SU has established an admissions presence in Los Angeles, California that will enhance the University’s visibility on the West Coast and will join the University’s West Coast offices of alumni relations, institutional advancement, and the LA semester program in the same location.</p> 
     <p>Syracuse University has also established an admissions presence in New York City and Atlanta, Georgia.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Art_collection">Art collection</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Syracuse_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Art collection">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>SU has a permanent art collection of over 45,000 objects from artists including Picasso, Rembrandt, Hopper, Tiffany and Wyeth. More than 100 important paintings, sculptures, and murals are displayed in public places around campus. Notable sculptures on campus include <a href="/wiki/Sol_LeWitt" title="Sol LeWitt">Sol LeWitt</a>'s <i>Six Curved Walls</i>, <a href="/wiki/Anna_Hyatt_Huntington" title="Anna Hyatt Huntington">Anna Hyatt Huntington</a>'s <i>Diana</i>, <a href="/wiki/Jean-Antoine_Houdon" title="Jean-Antoine Houdon">Jean-Antoine Houdon</a>'s <i>George Washington</i>, <a href="/wiki/Antoine_Bourdelle" title="Antoine Bourdelle">Antoine Bourdelle</a>'s <i>Herakles</i>, <a href="/wiki/James_Earle_Fraser_(sculptor)" title="James Earle Fraser (sculptor)">James Earle Fraser</a>'s <i>Lincoln</i>, <a href="/wiki/Malvina_Hoffman" title="Malvina Hoffman">Malvina Hoffman</a>'s <i>The Struggle of Elemental Man,</i> and <a href="/wiki/Ivan_Mestrovic" title="Ivan Mestrovic" class="mw-redirect">Ivan Mestrovic</a>'s <i>Moses</i>, <i>Job</i> and <i>Supplicant Persephone</i>.</p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Organization">Organization</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Syracuse_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Organization">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <p>Syracuse is governed by a 70 member Board of Trustees, with 64 trustees elected by the Board to four-year terms, and six elected by the alumni to four-year terms. Of the 64 Board elected Trustees, three must represent specified conferences of the <a href="/wiki/United_Methodist_Church" title="United Methodist Church">United Methodist Church</a>. In addition, the chancellor and the President of the Syracuse Alumni Association serve as ex officio voting Trustees. Two students and one faculty member serve as non-voting representatives to the Board of Trustees.<sup id="cite_ref-bylaws_56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bylaws-56"><span>[</span>56<span>]</span></a></sup> The Board of Trustees selects, and sets the salary of, the chancellor. The Syracuse University Bylaws also establish a University Senate with &quot;general supervision over all educational matters concerning the University as a whole....&quot; The Senate consists of administrators, faculty, students and staff.<sup id="cite_ref-bylaws_56-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bylaws-56"><span>[</span>56<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Academics">Academics</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Syracuse_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Academics">edit</a>]</span></h2>
