     <p>For the Class of 2012, there were approximately 25,000 applicants for 3,350 seats in the Freshman class.<sup id="cite_ref-Office_of_Admissions_64-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Office_of_Admissions-64"><span>[</span>64<span>]</span></a></sup> The libraries have collectively over 3.16 million volumes.<sup id="cite_ref-facts_4-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-facts-4"><span>[</span>4<span>]</span></a></sup> In fall 2006, the university had over 12,000 full-time undergraduate students and over 1,000 part-time undergraduate students, as well as almost 4,000 full-time graduate and law students and 2,000 part-time graduate and law students.<sup id="cite_ref-facts_4-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-facts-4"><span>[</span>4<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2005–06, the university granted over 2,600 bachelor's degrees; nearly 2,000 master's degrees; over 300 law degrees; and more than 160 doctoral degrees.<sup id="cite_ref-facts_4-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-facts-4"><span>[</span>4<span>]</span></a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/U.S._News_%26_World_Report" title="U.S. News &amp; World Report">U.S. News &amp; World Report</a></i> ranked SU 53rd among national universities in the United States for 2009 and 58th for 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-Best_Colleges_2009_65-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Best_Colleges_2009-65"><span>[</span>65<span>]</span></a></sup> Syracuse participates in the <a href="/wiki/National_Association_of_Independent_Colleges_and_Universities" title="National Association of Independent Colleges and Universities">National Association of Independent Colleges and Universities</a> and <a href="/wiki/University_and_College_Accountability_Network_(U-CAN)" title="University and College Accountability Network (U-CAN)" class="mw-redirect">University and College Accountability Network (U-CAN)</a>.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Degrees">Degrees</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Syracuse_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Degrees">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>SU offers undergraduate degrees in over 200 <a href="/wiki/Academic_major" title="Academic major">majors</a> in the 9 undergraduate schools and colleges.<sup id="cite_ref-Office_of_Admissions1_66-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Office_of_Admissions1-66"><span>[</span>66<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Bachelor%27s_degree" title="Bachelor's degree">Bachelor's degrees</a> are offered through the <a href="/wiki/Syracuse_University_School_of_Architecture" title="Syracuse University School of Architecture">Syracuse University School of Architecture</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Syracuse_University_College_of_Arts_and_Sciences" title="Syracuse University College of Arts and Sciences">College of Arts and Sciences</a>, the School of Education, the David B. Falk College of Sport and Human Dynamics, the L.C. Smith College of Engineering and Computer Science, the <a href="/wiki/Syracuse_University_School_of_Information_Studies" title="Syracuse University School of Information Studies">School of Information Studies</a>, <a href="/wiki/Martin_J._Whitman_School_of_Management" title="Martin J. Whitman School of Management">Martin J. Whitman School of Management</a>, <a href="/wiki/S.I._Newhouse_School_of_Public_Communications" title="S.I. Newhouse School of Public Communications" class="mw-redirect">S.I. Newhouse School of Public Communications</a>, and the College of Visual and Performing Arts. Also offered are <a href="/wiki/Master%27s_degree" title="Master's degree">Master's</a> and <a href="/wiki/Doctor_of_Philosophy" title="Doctor of Philosophy">doctoral</a> degrees from the Graduate School and from specialized programs in the <a href="/wiki/Maxwell_School_of_Citizenship_and_Public_Affairs" title="Maxwell School of Citizenship and Public Affairs">Maxwell School of Citizenship and Public Affairs</a>, <a href="/wiki/Syracuse_University_College_of_Law" title="Syracuse University College of Law">College of Law</a>, among others. Additionally, SU offers 24 Certificates of Advanced Study Programs for specialized programs for education, counseling, and other academic areas.<sup id="cite_ref-Graduate_School_Certificates_for_Advanced_Study_Programs_67-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Graduate_School_Certificates_for_Advanced_Study_Programs-67"><span>[</span>67<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The university has offered multiple international study programs since 1911. SU&nbsp;Abroad, formerly known as the Division of International Programs Abroad (DIPA), currently offers joint programs with universities in over 40 countries.<sup id="cite_ref-SUAbroad_68-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SUAbroad-68"><span>[</span>68<span>]</span></a></sup> The university operates eight international centers, called SU Abroad Centers, that offer structured programs in a variety of academic disciplines. The centers are located <a href="/wiki/Beijing" title="Beijing">Beijing</a>, <a href="/wiki/Istanbul" title="Istanbul">Istanbul</a>, <a href="/wiki/Florence,_Italy" title="Florence, Italy" class="mw-redirect">Florence, Italy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hong_Kong" title="Hong Kong">Hong Kong</a>, <a href="/wiki/London" title="London">London, UK</a>, <a href="/wiki/Madrid,_Spain" title="Madrid, Spain" class="mw-redirect">Madrid, Spain</a>, <a href="/wiki/Strasbourg,_France" title="Strasbourg, France" class="mw-redirect">Strasbourg, France</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Santiago,_Chile" title="Santiago, Chile" class="mw-redirect">Santiago, Chile</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-SUAbroad_68-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SUAbroad-68"><span>[</span>68<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-SU_Abroad.C2.A0.E2.80.93_Your_Place_In_The_World_69-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SU_Abroad.C2.A0.E2.80.93_Your_Place_In_The_World-69"><span>[</span>69<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="National_recognition_and_ranking">National recognition and ranking</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Syracuse_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: National recognition and ranking">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>In 2013, <i><a href="/wiki/U.S._News_%26_World_Report" title="U.S. News &amp; World Report">U.S. News &amp; World Report</a></i> ranked Syracuse number 58 among undergraduate national universities.<sup id="cite_ref-National_Universities_Ranking_70-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-National_Universities_Ranking-70"><span>[</span>70<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Many of SU's programs have been nationally recognized for excellence. A 2008 survey in the Academic Ranking of World Universities places Syracuse University in the top 100 world universities in social sciences.<sup id="cite_ref-Top_100_world_universities_in_Social_Sciences_71-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Top_100_world_universities_in_Social_Sciences-71"><span>[</span>71<span>]</span></a></sup> The industrial design program is ranked 3rd nationally by the 2012 issue of <i>DesignIntelligence</i>. The <a href="/wiki/Syracuse_University_School_of_Architecture" title="Syracuse University School of Architecture">School of Architecture's</a> Bachelor of Architecture program was ranked second nationally in 2010 by the journal <i>DesignIntelligence</i> in its annual edition of &quot;America's Best Architecture &amp; Design Schools.&quot;</p> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:292px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Newhouse_Communications_Center_III,_Syracuse_University.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Newhouse_Communications_Center_III%2C_Syracuse_University.JPG/290px-Newhouse_Communications_Center_III%2C_Syracuse_University.JPG" width="290" height="218" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Newhouse_Communications_Center_III%2C_Syracuse_University.JPG/435px-Newhouse_Communications_Center_III%2C_Syracuse_University.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Newhouse_Communications_Center_III%2C_Syracuse_University.JPG/580px-Newhouse_Communications_Center_III%2C_Syracuse_University.JPG 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Newhouse_Communications_Center_III,_Syracuse_University.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> Newhouse Communications Center III
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>The <a href="/wiki/S.I._Newhouse_School_of_Public_Communications" title="S.I. Newhouse School of Public Communications" class="mw-redirect">S.I. Newhouse School of Public Communications</a> is one of the top ranked in the country and has produced alumni in many fields of broadcasting.<sup id="cite_ref-Welcome_to_the_S.I._Newhouse_School_of_Public_Communications_72-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Welcome_to_the_S.I._Newhouse_School_of_Public_Communications-72"><span>[</span>72<span>]</span></a></sup> The School of Information Studies offers <a href="/wiki/Information_management" title="Information management">information management and technology</a> courses at the undergraduate level at Syracuse University. Within the school, <i><a href="/wiki/U.S._News_%26_World_Report" title="U.S. News &amp; World Report">U.S. News &amp; World Report</a></i> has ranked the graduate program as the third best in the United States. It also has the top-ranked undergraduate Information Systems program, the second ranked graduate program in Digital Librarianship, and the fourth ranked graduate program in School Library Media.<sup id="cite_ref-America.27s_Best_Graduate_Schools_73-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-America.27s_Best_Graduate_Schools-73"><span>[</span>73<span>]</span></a></sup> The College of Business Administration was renamed the <a href="/wiki/Martin_J._Whitman_School_of_Management" title="Martin J. Whitman School of Management">Martin J. Whitman School of Management</a> in 2003, in honor of SU alumnus and benefactor <a href="/wiki/Martin_J._Whitman" title="Martin J. Whitman">Martin J. Whitman</a>. The school is home to about 2,000 undergraduate and graduate students.</p> 
     <p>The undergraduate program was ranked No. 39 among business schools nationwide by <i>US News &amp; World Report</i> in 2008. The entrepreneurship program was ranked No. 8 by the <i>US News &amp; World Report</i> in 2008, and No. 13 by both <i>Entrepreneur Magazine</i> and <i>The Princeton Review</i> in 2007. The supply chain management program was ranked No. 10 in the nation by <i>Supply Chain Management Review</i>. Also, the Joseph I. Lubin School of Accounting was named No. 10 in the nation by <i>The Chronicle of Higher Education</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-fastfacts_74-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fastfacts-74"><span>[</span>74<span>]</span></a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Syracuse_University_College_of_Law" title="Syracuse University College of Law">College of Law</a> is ranked #86 nationally, and is ranked in the top 10 by <i>U.S. News and World Report</i> for its trial and appellate advocacy program and is an emerging leader in the relatively novel field of National Security Law.<sup id="cite_ref-INSCT.C2.A0.E2.80.93_Institute_for_National_Security_.26_Counterterrorism_75-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-INSCT.C2.A0.E2.80.93_Institute_for_National_Security_.26_Counterterrorism-75"><span>[</span>75<span>]</span></a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Maxwell_School_of_Citizenship_and_Public_Affairs" title="Maxwell School of Citizenship and Public Affairs">Maxwell School of Citizenship and Public Affairs</a> combines social sciences with public administration and international relations. It is ranked as the top graduate school for public affairs in the US.<sup id="cite_ref-Search.C2.A0.E2.80.93_Public_Affairs.C2.A0.E2.80.93_Best_Graduate_Schools.C2.A0.E2.80.93_Education.C2.A0.E2.80.93_US_News_and_World_Report_76-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Search.C2.A0.E2.80.93_Public_Affairs.C2.A0.E2.80.93_Best_Graduate_Schools.C2.A0.E2.80.93_Education.C2.A0.E2.80.93_US_News_and_World_Report-76"><span>[</span>76<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The graduate program of the College of Visual and Performing Art is considered one of the top 50 programs in the US.<sup id="cite_ref-Search.C2.A0.E2.80.93_Fine_Arts.C2.A0.E2.80.93_Best_Graduate_Schools.C2.A0.E2.80.93_Education.C2.A0.E2.80.93_US_News_and_World_Report_77-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Search.C2.A0.E2.80.93_Fine_Arts.C2.A0.E2.80.93_Best_Graduate_Schools.C2.A0.E2.80.93_Education.C2.A0.E2.80.93_US_News_and_World_Report-77"><span>[</span>77<span>]</span></a></sup> VPA ranked No. 14 in multimedia/visual communications, a specialty that includes disciplines found in the college’s Department of Transmedia, which offers M.F.A. programs in art photography, art video, computer art and film. VPA also ranked No. 16 in ceramics, No. 19 in printmaking and No. 20 in sculpture, which are M.F.A. programs based in the Department of Art. <a href="/wiki/Project_Advance" title="Project Advance">Project Advance</a> (or SUPA) is a nationally recognized concurrent enrollment program honored by the American Association for Higher Education, the Carnegie Foundation for the Advancement of Teaching, the National Commission on Excellence in Education, and the National Institute of Education.<sup id="cite_ref-SUPA_About_Us_78-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SUPA_About_Us-78"><span>[</span>78<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Faculty">Faculty</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Syracuse_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Faculty">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="thumb tleft"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Slutzker_Center,_Syracuse_University.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Slutzker_Center%2C_Syracuse_University.JPG/300px-Slutzker_Center%2C_Syracuse_University.JPG" width="300" height="225" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Slutzker_Center%2C_Syracuse_University.JPG/450px-Slutzker_Center%2C_Syracuse_University.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Slutzker_Center%2C_Syracuse_University.JPG/600px-Slutzker_Center%2C_Syracuse_University.JPG 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Slutzker_Center,_Syracuse_University.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> Slutzker Center for International Services.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>Syracuse University has 1013 full-time instructional faculty, 96 part-time faculty, and 454 <a href="/wiki/Adjunct_faculty" title="Adjunct faculty" class="mw-redirect">adjunct faculty</a>. Approximately 86% of the full-time faculty have earned Ph.D.'s or professional degrees.<sup id="cite_ref-fc_3-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fc-3"><span>[</span>3<span>]</span></a></sup> The current faculty includes scholars such as <a href="/wiki/United_States_National_Academy_of_Sciences" title="United States National Academy of Sciences" class="mw-redirect">United States National Academy of Sciences</a> member Jozef J. Zwislocki, Professor of Psychology, who developed mathematical models on the mechanics of the <a href="/wiki/Inner_ear" title="Inner ear">inner</a> and <a href="/wiki/Middle_ear" title="Middle ear">middle ear</a>, <a href="/wiki/MacArthur_Fellow" title="MacArthur Fellow" class="mw-redirect">MacArthur Fellow</a> <a href="/wiki/Don_Mitchell_(geographer)" title="Don Mitchell (geographer)">Don Mitchell</a>, Professor of Geography, who has developed studies in cultural geography, <a href="/wiki/Bruce_Kingma" title="Bruce Kingma">Bruce Kingma</a>, Associate Provost and Kauffman Professor of Entrepreneurship, a pioneer in the field of information economics and online learning, <a href="/wiki/Catherine_Bertini" title="Catherine Bertini">Catherine Bertini</a>, Professor of Practice in Public Administration, who has worked on the role of women in food distribution, <a href="/wiki/Frederick_C._Beiser" title="Frederick C. Beiser">Frederick C. Beiser</a>, Professor of Philosophy, one of leading scholars of <a href="/wiki/German_idealism" title="German idealism">German idealism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mary_Karr" title="Mary Karr">Mary Karr</a>, the Jesse Truesdell Peck Professor of Literature, who has received a <a href="/wiki/Guggenheim_Fellowship" title="Guggenheim Fellowship">Guggenheim Fellowship</a> in poetry, <a href="/wiki/John_Caputo" title="John Caputo" class="mw-redirect">John Caputo</a>, the Thomas J. Watson Professor of Humanities, who founded <a href="/wiki/Weak_theology" title="Weak theology" class="mw-redirect">weak theology</a>, and Gustav Niebuhr Associate Professor of Religion and Media who is the former <a href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times" title="The New York Times">New York Times</a> National Religion Correspondent.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Syracuse_University_Press">Syracuse University Press</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Syracuse_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Syracuse University Press">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/Syracuse_University_Press" title="Syracuse University Press">Syracuse University Press</a>
     </div> 
     <p>Founded on August 2, 1943 by Chancellor William Pearson Tolley and benefactor <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Watson,_Sr." title="Thomas Watson, Sr." class="mw-redirect">Thomas Watson, Sr.</a> The areas of focus for the Press include Middle East Studies, Native American Studies, Peace and Conflict Resolution, Irish Studies and Jewish Studies, among others. The Press has an international reputation in Irish Studies and Middle East Studies. It is a member of the Association of American University Presses.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="University_lectures">University lectures</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Syracuse_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: University lectures">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>Every year as a tradition, the University would invite notable and influential speakers from around the world. These speakers have moved the world in various ways in the areas of sustainability, advertising, redevelopment, human rights, journalism, and the environment. The lecturers have been held to the highest standard in academic and public service excellence. The University Lectures are supported by the University Trustees, alumni, and friends.<sup id="cite_ref-University_lectures_79-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-University_lectures-79"><span>[</span>79<span>]</span></a></sup> Previous University lecturers included <a href="/wiki/Ishmael_Beah" title="Ishmael Beah">Ishmael Beah</a>, author of &quot;<a href="/wiki/A_Long_Way_Gone:_Memoirs_of_a_Boy_Soldier" title="A Long Way Gone: Memoirs of a Boy Soldier">A Long Way Gone: Memoirs of a Boy Soldier</a>&quot;, 45th <a href="/wiki/Vice_President_of_the_United_States" title="Vice President of the United States">Vice President of the United States</a>, <a href="/wiki/Al_Gore" title="Al Gore">Al Gore</a>, Economist and <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize" title="Nobel Prize">Nobel Prize</a> winner, <a href="/wiki/Muhammad_Yunus" title="Muhammad Yunus">Muhammad Yunus</a>, author and columnist, <a href="/wiki/William_Safire" title="William Safire">William Safire</a>, environmental justice advocate <a href="/wiki/Majora_Carter" title="Majora Carter">Majora Carter</a>, and environmental law attorney, <a href="/wiki/Robert_Kennedy_Jr." title="Robert Kennedy Jr." class="mw-redirect">Robert Kennedy Jr.</a><sup id="cite_ref-University_lectures2_80-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-University_lectures2-80"><span>[</span>80<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Library">Library</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Syracuse_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Library">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Syracuse_Carnegie_Library.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Syracuse_Carnegie_Library.jpg/250px-Syracuse_Carnegie_Library.jpg" width="250" height="187" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Syracuse_Carnegie_Library.jpg/375px-Syracuse_Carnegie_Library.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Syracuse_Carnegie_Library.jpg/500px-Syracuse_Carnegie_Library.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Syracuse_Carnegie_Library.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> The Carnegie Library
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>Syracuse University's main library is the Ernest S. Bird Library, which opened in 1972. Its seven levels contain 2.3 million books, 11,500 periodicals, 45,000 feet (14,000&nbsp;m) of manuscripts and rare books, 3.6 million <a href="/wiki/Microform" title="Microform">microforms</a>, and a caf&eacute;. There are also several departmental libraries on campus. Many of the landmarks in the history of recorded communication between people are in the university's Special Collections Research Center, from <a href="/wiki/Cuneiform" title="Cuneiform">cuneiform</a> tablets and papyri to several codices dating from the 11th century, to the invention of printing. The collection also includes works by <a href="/wiki/Galileo" title="Galileo" class="mw-redirect">Galileo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Martin_Luther" title="Martin Luther">Luther</a>, <a href="/wiki/John_Calvin" title="John Calvin">John Calvin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Voltaire" title="Voltaire">Voltaire</a>, Sir <a href="/wiki/Isaac_Newton" title="Isaac Newton">Isaac Newton</a>, <a href="/wiki/Descartes" title="Descartes" class="mw-redirect">Descartes</a>, Sir <a href="/wiki/Francis_Bacon" title="Francis Bacon">Francis Bacon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Samuel_Johnson" title="Samuel Johnson">Samuel Johnson</a>, <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Hobbes" title="Thomas Hobbes">Thomas Hobbes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Goethe" title="Goethe" class="mw-redirect">Goethe</a>, and others. In addition, the collection includes the personal library of <a href="/wiki/Leopold_Von_Ranke" title="Leopold Von Ranke" class="mw-redirect">Leopold Von Ranke</a>.</p> 
     <p>Making sensational headlines at the time, the university outbid the Prussian government for all 19 tons of Von Ranke's prized personal library. Other collections of note include Rudyard Kipling first editions and an original second leaf of the Gutenberg Bible. The university is also home to the Belfer Audio Laboratory and Archive, whose holdings total approximately 540,000 recordings in all formats, primarily cylinders, discs, and magnetic tapes. Some of the voices to be found include <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Edison" title="Thomas Edison">Thomas Edison</a>, <a href="/wiki/Amelia_Earhart" title="Amelia Earhart">Amelia Earhart</a>, <a href="/wiki/Albert_Einstein" title="Albert Einstein">Albert Einstein</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Oscar_Wilde" title="Oscar Wilde">Oscar Wilde</a>. Bird Library is also home to the largest collection of national archives of <a href="/wiki/Kenya" title="Kenya">Kenya</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tanzania" title="Tanzania">Tanzania</a>. In July 2008, Syracuse University became the owner of the second largest collection of 78&nbsp;rpm records in the United States after the <a href="/wiki/Library_of_Congress" title="Library of Congress">Library of Congress</a> after a donation of more than 200,000 records. The donation is valued at $1&nbsp;million and more than doubles the University's collection of 78&nbsp;rpm records to about 400,000.<sup id="cite_ref-records_81-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-records-81"><span>[</span>81<span>]</span></a></sup> It also has a special The Harriet Tubman Research Collection, and Environmental Justice and Gender collection housed in the <a href="/wiki/Department_of_African_American_Studies_-_Syracuse_University#Martin_Luther_King_Jr._Memorial_Library" title="Department of African American Studies - Syracuse University" class="mw-redirect">Martin Luther King Jr. Memorial Library</a>. The MLK library holds over 15,000 acquisitions in African, African-American, Afro-Lationo, and Caribbean studies.</p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Research">Research</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Syracuse_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Research">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <p>According to the <a href="/wiki/Carnegie_Classification_of_Institutions_of_Higher_Education" title="Carnegie Classification of Institutions of Higher Education">Carnegie Classification of Institutions of Higher Education</a>, Syracuse University is a research university with a high level of research activity.<sup id="cite_ref-Institutions:_Syracuse_University_82-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Institutions:_Syracuse_University-82"><span>[</span>82<span>]</span></a></sup> Through the university's Office of Research, which promotes research, technology transfer, and scholarship, and its Office of Sponsored Programs, which assists faculty in seeking and obtaining external research support, SU supports research in the fields of management and business, sciences, engineering, education, information studies, energy, environment, communications, computer science, public and international affairs, and other specialized areas.<sup id="cite_ref-Syracuse_University_Research_83-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Syracuse_University_Research-83"><span>[</span>83<span>]</span></a></sup> Syracuse became a member of the <a href="/wiki/Association_of_American_Universities" title="Association of American Universities">Association of American Universities</a> (AAU) in 1966, an organization of leading research universities devoted to maintaining a strong system of research and education.<sup id="cite_ref-Association_of_American_Universities_Member_Institutions_84-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Association_of_American_Universities_Member_Institutions-84"><span>[</span>84<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2011, however, the university's board of trustees voted to pull out of the research consortium.<sup id="cite_ref-selingo20110502_85-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-selingo20110502-85"><span>[</span>85<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <div class="thumb tleft"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Holden_Observatory,_Syracuse_University.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Holden_Observatory%2C_Syracuse_University.jpg/300px-Holden_Observatory%2C_Syracuse_University.jpg" width="300" height="225" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Holden_Observatory%2C_Syracuse_University.jpg/450px-Holden_Observatory%2C_Syracuse_University.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Holden_Observatory%2C_Syracuse_University.jpg/600px-Holden_Observatory%2C_Syracuse_University.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Holden_Observatory,_Syracuse_University.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> Holden Observatory which houses the University's State Recorder's office. 
        <strong class="selflink">Syracuse University</strong>.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>SU has established 29 research centers and institutes that focuses research, often across disciplines, in a variety of areas.<sup id="cite_ref-sucenter_86-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sucenter-86"><span>[</span>86<span>]</span></a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Burton_Blatt_Institute" title="Burton Blatt Institute">Burton Blatt Institute</a> advances research in economic and social issues for individuals with disabilities, and it has international projects in the field.<sup id="cite_ref-Burton_Blatt_Institute:_BBI_Projects_87-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Burton_Blatt_Institute:_BBI_Projects-87"><span>[</span>87<span>]</span></a></sup> The Martin J Whitman School of Management supports the largest number of research centers, including The Ballentine Investment Institute, the George E. Bennett Center for Accounting and Tax Research, the Robert H. Brethren Operations Management Institute, Michael J. Falcone Center for Entrepreneurship, The H. H. Franklin Center for Supply Chain Management, Olivia and Walter Kiebach Center for International Business Studies, and the Earl V. Snyder Innovation Management Program.</p> 
     <p>Other research programs include The Syracuse Biomaterials Institute, the Alan K. Campbell Public Affairs Institute through the Maxwell School, and the Center for the Study of Popular Television through the Newhouse School of Public Communications.<sup id="cite_ref-sucenter_86-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sucenter-86"><span>[</span>86<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Syracuse University also has collaborations with CERN and Fermi National Accelerator Laboratory, among other institutes.</p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Student_life">Student life</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Syracuse_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Student life">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <p>Syracuse University has a diverse student population, representing all 50 US states and over 115 countries. Approximately 10 percent of students are from outside of the US, and are supported by an international services department within the University's Division of Student Affairs.<sup id="cite_ref-Center_for_International_Services_88-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Center_for_International_Services-88"><span>[</span>88<span>]</span></a></sup> Approximately 37% of students in the fall 2010 undergraduate full-time class are from New York State. Approximately 56% of that class are women.<sup id="cite_ref-Syracuse_University_Facts-Student_Demographics_89-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Syracuse_University_Facts-Student_Demographics-89"><span>[</span>89<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Media">Media</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Syracuse_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Media">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <table class="metadata plainlinks ambox ambox-content ambox-Unreferenced" style=""> 
      <tbody>
       <tr> 
        <td class="mbox-image"> 
         <div style="width: 52px;">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="image"><img alt="Question book-new.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" width="50" height="39" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" /></a>
         </div> </td> 
        <td class="mbox-text" style=""><span class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>does not <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources">cite</a> any <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">references or sources</a></b>. <span class="hide-when-compact">Please help improve this section by <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing/1">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability#Burden_of_evidence" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">removed</a>.</span> <small><i>(April 2011)</i></small> </span></td> 
       </tr> 
      </tbody>
     </table> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:272px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:CitrusTV_controlroom.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/8/82/CitrusTV_controlroom.jpg" width="270" height="180" class="thumbimage" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:CitrusTV_controlroom.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> The CitrusTV control room during a taping of CitrusTV News
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p><a href="/wiki/CitrusTV" title="CitrusTV">CitrusTV</a> (formerly UUTV, HillTV and Synapse) is the university's entirely student-run television studio, and one of the largest student-run TV studios in the country with over 300 active members.<sup id="cite_ref-Citrus-members_90-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Citrus-members-90"><span>[</span>90<span>]</span></a></sup> CitrusTV produces news, sports, and entertainment content that appears on the university's campus cable channel, the <a href="/wiki/Orange_Television_Network" title="Orange Television Network">Orange Television Network</a>, and online on the CitrusTV.net website. Some content also appears in Central New York on the cable channel <a href="/wiki/Time_Warner_Cable_Sports" title="Time Warner Cable Sports" class="mw-redirect">Time Warner Cable Sports</a>. The station used to be a part of University Union, the largest student organization on campus<sup class="Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="reliable source needed for the statistic (June 2011)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>, until it split to become its own recognized student organization in 2004. The station was briefly known as HillTV until the middle of the fall 2005 semester, when the university temporarily shut the station down for a controversial entertainment episode and demanded its reform. The station is located in the Robert B. Menschel Media Center, at the Waverly Avenue side of Watson Hall.</p> 
     <p>The <a href="/wiki/Orange_Television_Network" title="Orange Television Network">Orange Television Network</a> is the university-controlled campus cable TV station. It is available on channel 2 in all campus buildings, and on channel 2.1 in high definition.</p> 
     <p>The school's independent student newspaper is <i><a href="/wiki/The_Daily_Orange" title="The Daily Orange">The Daily Orange</a></i>, founded in 1903 and independent since 1971. The D.O. Alumni Association recently celebrated the paper's 100th anniversary.</p> 
     <p><a href="/wiki/WAER" title="WAER">WAER</a> (88.3 <a href="/wiki/FM_broadcasting" title="FM broadcasting">FM</a>) is located on the campus of SU, and is an auxiliary service of the school. The station features a jazz music and <a href="/wiki/National_Public_Radio" title="National Public Radio" class="mw-redirect">National Public Radio</a> format, with a news and music staff providing 24-hour programming. It is best known for its sports staff, which has produced the likes of <a href="/wiki/Bob_Costas" title="Bob Costas">Bob Costas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Marv_Albert" title="Marv Albert">Marv Albert</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mike_Tirico" title="Mike Tirico">Mike Tirico</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sean_McDonough" title="Sean McDonough">Sean McDonough</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ian_Eagle" title="Ian Eagle">Ian Eagle</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brian_Higgins" title="Brian Higgins">Brian Higgins</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Dick_Stockton" title="Dick Stockton">Dick Stockton</a>. <a href="/wiki/Lou_Reed" title="Lou Reed">Lou Reed</a> also hosted a free-format show on WAER during his time at Syracuse University; this free-format radio tradition at Syracuse is carried on by WERW.</p> 
     <p><a href="/wiki/WJPZ" title="WJPZ" class="mw-redirect">WJPZ</a> is a radio station owned and operated entirely by SU students. It broadcasts at 89.1 FM at an effective radiated power of 100 watts and can be heard throughout Syracuse, the rest of Onondaga County, and beyond to the north and east. WJPZ programs a tight CHR (Contemporary Hit Radio, or Top 40) format. Although operated by students, it is an independent organization which is incorporated and licensed by the FCC as WJPZ Radio, Inc. It is neither owned nor controlled by Syracuse University, but it does lease studio and transmitter facilities on Syracuse University property.</p> 
     <p><a href="/wiki/WERW" title="WERW">WERW</a> is the entirely student-run, free format <a href="/wiki/Carrier_current" title="Carrier current">carrier current</a> <a href="/wiki/Radio_station" title="Radio station" class="mw-redirect">radio station</a> on the SU campus. It is the only campus radio station currently being broadcast on iTunes college radio. The station can also be heard at 1570 AM. The studios are located in the Schine Student Center. Originally operating at 750AM, WERW was available only in the university's dorms and some other campus buildings. The station's current low power broadcast tower was erected atop the Booth Hall dormitory in 1995 to allow it to broadcast at 1570AM. With this new tower, WERW could be heard all across the university campus and in adjacent areas of the city of Syracuse.</p> 
     <p>There are also multiple student-run magazines and other print publications, including: The Onondagan Yearbook, Student Voice, Jerk Magazine, What the Health, 360, and Equal Time.<sup id="cite_ref-Ed2010_91-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ed2010-91"><span>[</span>91<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Student_government">Student government</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Syracuse_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Student government">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>Founded in 1957, the Student Association (SA) represents the undergraduate students of both SU and ESF. The SA, through the Student Assembly, oversees the allocation and designation of the Student Activity Fee that was first collected in the 1968–69 school year. The goals of the SA are to participate through a unified student voice in the formulation of Syracuse University rules and regulations. The SA-SGA Alumni Organization maintains the history and an organizational timeline on its website.<sup id="cite_ref-Student_Association_92-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Student_Association-92"><span>[</span>92<span>]</span></a></sup> Students elect two non-voting representatives to the Board of Trustees.<sup id="cite_ref-bylaws_56-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bylaws-56"><span>[</span>56<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The graduate students at Syracuse University are represented by the Graduate Student Organization (GSO) while the law students at Syracuse University are represented by the Law Student Senate. Each of the three organizations elects students to serve in the Syracuse University Senate, which also includes faculty and staff and is chaired by the SU Chancellor.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Fraternities_and_sororities">Fraternities and sororities</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Syracuse_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Fraternities and sororities">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/Syracuse_University_fraternity_and_sorority_system" title="Syracuse University fraternity and sorority system">Syracuse University fraternity and sorority system</a>
     </div> 
     <p>The Syracuse University <a href="/wiki/Fraternities_and_sororities" title="Fraternities and sororities" class="mw-redirect">fraternity</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sorority" title="Sorority" class="mw-redirect">sorority</a> system offers organizations that are members of the <a href="/wiki/National_Panhellenic_Conference" title="National Panhellenic Conference">Panhellenic Council</a> (NPC), the <a href="/wiki/North-American_Interfraternity_Conference" title="North-American Interfraternity Conference">Interfraternity Council</a> (IFC), the <a href="/wiki/National_Association_of_Latino_Fraternal_Organizations" title="National Association of Latino Fraternal Organizations">National Association of Latino Fraternal Organizations</a>, the <a href="/wiki/National_Multicultural_Greek_Council" title="National Multicultural Greek Council">National Multicultural Greek Council</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/National_Pan-Hellenic_Council" title="National Pan-Hellenic Council">National Pan-Hellenic Council</a> (NPHC). In addition to SU students, ESF students are permitted to join the university's fraternity and sorority system.</p> 
     <p>The oldest fraternity at SU is <a href="/wiki/Delta_Kappa_Epsilon" title="Delta Kappa Epsilon">Delta Kappa Epsilon</a>, which established a chapter in 1871 soon after the founding of the university, followed by <a href="/wiki/Psi_Upsilon" title="Psi Upsilon">Psi Upsilon</a> in 1875 and <a href="/wiki/Phi_Kappa_Psi" title="Phi Kappa Psi">Phi Kappa Psi</a> in 1884.<sup id="cite_ref-greekhistory_93-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-greekhistory-93"><span>[</span>93<span>]</span></a></sup> Sororities were also a part of the early history of SU. <a href="/wiki/Alpha_Phi" title="Alpha Phi">Alpha Phi</a> was founded at SU in 1872, followed by <a href="/wiki/Gamma_Phi_Beta" title="Gamma Phi Beta">Gamma Phi Beta</a> in 1874 and <a href="/wiki/Alpha_Gamma_Delta" title="Alpha Gamma Delta">Alpha Gamma Delta</a> in 1904. <a href="/wiki/Alpha_Phi_Alpha" title="Alpha Phi Alpha">Alpha Phi Alpha</a> established a chapter at SU in 1910, and was reorganized in 1949 and 1973.<sup id="cite_ref-Alpha_Phi_Alpha.C2.A0.E2.80.94_Delta_Zeta_Chapter.C2.A0.E2.80.94_Syracuse_University_94-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Alpha_Phi_Alpha.C2.A0.E2.80.94_Delta_Zeta_Chapter.C2.A0.E2.80.94_Syracuse_University-94"><span>[</span>94<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Alpha_Phi_Delta" title="Alpha Phi Delta">Alpha Phi Delta</a>, the only historically Italian-American heritage fraternity, was founded at SU in 1914. The first NPHC fraternity, <a href="/wiki/Omega_Psi_Phi" title="Omega Psi Phi">Omega Psi Phi</a>, was established at SU in 1922, and the first NPHC sorority, <a href="/wiki/Delta_Sigma_Theta" title="Delta Sigma Theta">Delta Sigma Theta</a> in 1973.<sup id="cite_ref-greekhistory_93-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-greekhistory-93"><span>[</span>93<span>]</span></a></sup> University policy prohibits fraternities and sororities from discriminating &quot;on the basis of race, creed, color, gender, national origin, religion, marital status, age, disability, sexual orientation, or status as a disabled veteran or a veteran of the Vietnam era.&quot;<sup id="cite_ref-Chapter_Development_Plan_95-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Chapter_Development_Plan-95"><span>[</span>95<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Syracuse_University_Ambulance">Syracuse University Ambulance</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Syracuse_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Syracuse University Ambulance">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://sua.syr.edu/">Syracuse University Ambulance</a>, commonly referred to as SUA, is a SU Health Services-based student organization that responds to over 1,500 medical emergencies each year. Providing <a href="/wiki/Basic_life_support" title="Basic life support">basic life support</a> (BLS), rapid cardiac <a href="/wiki/Defibrillation" title="Defibrillation">defibrillation</a>, emergent and non-emergent transportation, and special event standby services, SUA operates two full-time transporting ambulances, a supervisor's fly car, and a MCI trailer for <a href="/wiki/Mass-casualty_incident" title="Mass-casualty incident">mass-casualty incidents</a>. Additionally, SUA operates four transport vans for non-emergency transports. <a href="/wiki/Advanced_life_support" title="Advanced life support">Advanced life support</a> (ALS) mutual aid is provided by the City of Syracuse's private <a href="/wiki/Emergency_medical_services" title="Emergency medical services">EMS</a> provider, <a href="/wiki/Rural/Metro" title="Rural/Metro" class="mw-redirect">Rural/Metro</a> Medical Services. SUA was formed in 1973 by a group of students out of a need for emergency medical services on campus. Starting with only a few members and meager equipment, the Syracuse University Medical Crisis Unit was formed. The organization has evolved greatly over time but, with 70+ volunteer students, remains a student-run organization to this day. SUA provides emergency and non-emergency services 24-hours a day, 7-days a week during the academic school year and is funded by a portion of the student health fee.</p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Athletics">Athletics</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Syracuse_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Athletics">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/Syracuse_Orange" title="Syracuse Orange">Syracuse Orange</a>
     </div> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Syracuse_Football_2005_Opener.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Syracuse_Football_2005_Opener.jpg/250px-Syracuse_Football_2005_Opener.jpg" width="250" height="188" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Syracuse_Football_2005_Opener.jpg/375px-Syracuse_Football_2005_Opener.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Syracuse_Football_2005_Opener.jpg/500px-Syracuse_Football_2005_Opener.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Syracuse_Football_2005_Opener.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> Syracuse Orange football team entering the 
        <a href="/wiki/Carrier_Dome" title="Carrier Dome">Carrier Dome</a>.

     <p>Syracuse University's sports teams have &quot;the Orange&quot; nickname since 2004, although the former names of Orangemen and Orangewomen are still used. The school's mascot is <a href="/wiki/Otto_the_Orange" title="Otto the Orange">Otto the Orange</a>. SU fields intercollegiate teams in eight men's sports and 12 women's sports, but they do not sponsor a Baseball program in the Atlantic Coast Conference.</p> 
     <p>Most of Syracuse University's intercollegiate teams participate in <a href="/wiki/National_Collegiate_Athletic_Association" title="National Collegiate Athletic Association">NCAA</a> <a href="/wiki/Division_I_(NCAA)" title="Division I (NCAA)">Division I</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Coast_Conference" title="Atlantic Coast Conference">Atlantic Coast Conference</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Syracuse_Orange_women%27s_ice_hockey" title="Syracuse Orange women's ice hockey">Syracuse Orange women's ice hockey</a> team participates in <a href="/wiki/College_Hockey_America" title="College Hockey America">College Hockey America</a>. <a href="/wiki/College_rowing_(United_States)" title="College rowing (United States)">Crew</a> participates in the <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Association_of_Rowing_Colleges" title="Eastern Association of Rowing Colleges">Eastern Association of Rowing Colleges</a>. The men's and women's basketball teams, the football team, and both the men's and women's lacrosse teams play in the <a href="/wiki/Carrier_Dome" title="Carrier Dome">Carrier Dome</a>. Other sports are located at the nearby <a href="/wiki/Manley_Field_House" title="Manley Field House">Manley Field House</a>, except ice hockey which takes place in the <a href="/wiki/Tennity_Ice_Skating_Pavilion" title="Tennity Ice Skating Pavilion">Tennity Ice Skating Pavilion</a>.</p> 
     <p>SU has reached 28 team national championships, including 14 men's lacrosse, six men's crew, two <a href="/wiki/Cross_country_running" title="Cross country running">cross country running</a>, and one each in <a href="/wiki/Boxing" title="Boxing">boxing</a>, <a href="/wiki/College_football" title="College football">football</a>, and women's lacrosse.<sup id="cite_ref-SU_Athletics.C2.A0.E2.80.93_Syracuse_National_Champions_96-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SU_Athletics.C2.A0.E2.80.93_Syracuse_National_Champions-96"><span>[</span>96<span>]</span></a></sup> Under long-time head coach <a href="/wiki/Jim_Boeheim" title="Jim Boeheim">Jim Boeheim</a>, <a href="/wiki/Syracuse_Orange_men%27s_basketball" title="Syracuse Orange men's basketball">men's basketball team</a> won seven <a href="/wiki/Big_East_Conference_(1979%E2%80%932013)" title="Big East Conference (1979–2013)">Big East</a> regular season championships, five <a href="/wiki/Big_East_Men%27s_Basketball_Tournament" title="Big East Men's Basketball Tournament">Big East Tournament</a> championships, and 25 <a href="/wiki/NCAA_Men%27s_Division_I_Basketball_Championship" title="NCAA Men's Division I Basketball Championship">NCAA Tournament</a> appearances, including the <a href="/wiki/2003_NCAA_Men%27s_Division_I_Basketball_Tournament" title="2003 NCAA Men's Division I Basketball Tournament">2003 NCAA championship</a>. The men's basketball team holds the largest on campus attendance record of 35,012 attendees. The record was set in the Carrier Dome playing Georgetown on Sat March 2, 2013.</p> 
     <div class="thumb tleft"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Syracuse_lacrosse_at_the_WH.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/Syracuse_lacrosse_at_the_WH.jpg/300px-Syracuse_lacrosse_at_the_WH.jpg" width="300" height="180" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/Syracuse_lacrosse_at_the_WH.jpg/450px-Syracuse_lacrosse_at_the_WH.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/f/f5/Syracuse_lacrosse_at_the_WH.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Syracuse_lacrosse_at_the_WH.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> The 
        <a href="/wiki/Syracuse_Orange_men%27s_lacrosse" title="Syracuse Orange men's lacrosse">Syracuse University Orange men's lacrosse team</a> are honored at the 
        <a href="/wiki/White_House" title="White House">White House</a> by 
        <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_United_States" title="President of the United States">President of the United States</a> 
        <a href="/wiki/George_W._Bush" title="George W. Bush">George W. Bush</a> for their winning the 
        <a href="/wiki/2008_NCAA_Division_I_Men%27s_Lacrosse_Championship" title="2008 NCAA Division I Men's Lacrosse Championship">2008 National Collegiate Athletic Association Division I national championship</a>.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>In 1959, Syracuse earned its first <a href="/wiki/NCAA_Division_I-A_national_football_champions" title="NCAA Division I-A national football champions" class="mw-redirect">National Championship</a> following an undefeated football season and a Cotton Bowl victory over <a href="/wiki/University_of_Texas_at_Austin" title="University of Texas at Austin">Texas</a>. The team featured sophomore running back <a href="/wiki/Ernie_Davis" title="Ernie Davis">Ernie Davis</a> who, in 1961, became the first African-American to win the <a href="/wiki/Heisman_Trophy" title="Heisman Trophy">Heisman Trophy</a>. Davis was slated to play for the <a href="/wiki/Cleveland_Browns" title="Cleveland Browns">Cleveland Browns</a> in the same backfield as <a href="/wiki/Jim_Brown" title="Jim Brown">Jim Brown</a>, but died of <a href="/wiki/Leukemia" title="Leukemia">leukemia</a> before being able to play professionally.<sup id="cite_ref-cityofelmira_97-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cityofelmira-97"><span>[</span>97<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Syracuse played its first intercollegiate lacrosse game in 1916, and captured its first USILA championship in 1920. It won USILA championships in 1922, 1924, and 1925. In the modern NCAA era, Syracuse is the first school to capture 11 National Championships, the most of any team in college lacrosse history. Syracuse currently won two men's Div I lacrosse championships in 2008 and 2009 seasons, and reached the quarterfinals in 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-suathletics_98-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-suathletics-98"><span>[</span>98<span>]</span></a></sup> The women's lacrosse team reached the NCAA Division I National Championship game for the first time in school history in 2012, which they lost to Northwestern.</p> 
     <p>Toward the end of the 1970s, Syracuse University was under pressure to improve its football facilities in order to remain a NCAA Division I football school. Its small concrete stadium, <a href="/wiki/Archbold_Stadium" title="Archbold Stadium">Archbold Stadium</a>, was seventy years old and not up to the standards of other schools. The stadium could not be expanded; it had been reduced from 40,000 seats to 26,000 due to the fire codes. Syracuse University decided to build a new stadium. In 1978, Archbold Stadium was demolished to make way for the Carrier Dome, which was to have a domed <a href="/wiki/Teflon" title="Teflon" class="mw-redirect">Teflon</a>-coated, <a href="/wiki/Fiberglass" title="Fiberglass">fiberglass</a> <a href="/wiki/Air-supported_structure" title="Air-supported structure">inflatable roof</a>. It would also serve as the home for the men's basketball team, as a replacement for Manley Field House. The Carrier Dome was constructed between April 1979 and September 1980. The total construction cost was $26.85&nbsp;million, including a $2.75&nbsp;million <a href="/wiki/Naming_rights" title="Naming rights">naming gift</a> from the <a href="/wiki/Carrier_Corporation" title="Carrier Corporation">Carrier Corporation</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Carrier_100th_Anniversary:_Dome_Sweet_Dome_99-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Carrier_100th_Anniversary:_Dome_Sweet_Dome-99"><span>[</span>99<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Alumni">Alumni</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Syracuse_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Alumni">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/List_of_Syracuse_University_people#Notable_alumni" title="List of Syracuse University people">List of Syracuse University people#Notable alumni</a>
     </div> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">

        <a href="/wiki/Joe_Biden" title="Joe Biden">Joe Biden</a> 
        <a href="/wiki/Juris_Doctor" title="Juris Doctor">J.D.</a> '68,

       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>Among the individuals who have attended or graduated from Syracuse University include novelists <a href="/wiki/Stephen_Crane" title="Stephen Crane">Stephen Crane</a>, <a href="/wiki/Joyce_Carol_Oates" title="Joyce Carol Oates">Joyce Carol Oates</a>, <a href="/wiki/John_D._MacDonald" title="John D. MacDonald">John D. MacDonald</a>, <a href="/wiki/Shirley_Jackson" title="Shirley Jackson">Shirley Jackson</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Alice_Sebold" title="Alice Sebold">Alice Sebold</a>; <a href="/wiki/William_Safire" title="William Safire">William Safire</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pulitzer_Prize" title="Pulitzer Prize">Pulitzer Prize</a> winning commentator; Cambridge University historian Sir <a href="/wiki/Moses_I._Finley" title="Moses I. Finley">Moses I. Finley</a>; <a href="/wiki/Arthur_Rock" title="Arthur Rock">Arthur Rock</a>, legendary venture capitalist and cofounder of Intel; <a href="/wiki/Donna_Shalala" title="Donna Shalala">Donna Shalala</a>, former <a href="/wiki/United_States_Secretary_of_Health_and_Human_Services" title="United States Secretary of Health and Human Services">United States Secretary of Health and Human Services</a>; <a href="/wiki/Joe_Biden" title="Joe Biden">Joe Biden</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vice_President_of_the_United_States" title="Vice President of the United States">Vice President of the United States</a>; <a href="/wiki/Robert_Jarvik" title="Robert Jarvik">Robert Jarvik</a>, inventor of the first <a href="/wiki/Artificial_heart" title="Artificial heart">artificial heart</a> implanted into human beings; <a href="/wiki/Eileen_Collins" title="Eileen Collins">Eileen Collins</a>, first female commander of a <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle_program" title="Space Shuttle program">Space Shuttle</a>; Prince <a href="/wiki/Sultan_bin_Salman" title="Sultan bin Salman" class="mw-redirect">Sultan bin Salman</a>, first Arab, first Muslim and the youngest person to travel to space; Robert Menschel, legendary partner/director at <a href="/wiki/Goldman_Sachs" title="Goldman Sachs">Goldman Sachs</a>; musician <a href="/wiki/Lou_Reed" title="Lou Reed">Lou Reed</a>; and Prince <a href="/wiki/Al-Waleed_bin_Talal" title="Al-Waleed bin Talal">Al-Waleed bin Talal</a>, a prominent investor and member of the <a href="/wiki/Saudi_Arabia" title="Saudi Arabia">Saudi</a> <a href="/wiki/House_of_Saud" title="House of Saud">royal family</a>.</p> 
     <p>The S.I. Newhouse School of Public Communications has produced several alumni in broadcasting including <a href="/wiki/Bob_Costas" title="Bob Costas">Bob Costas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Len_Berman" title="Len Berman">Len Berman</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sean_McDonough" title="Sean McDonough">Sean McDonough</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mike_Tirico" title="Mike Tirico">Mike Tirico</a>, <a href="/wiki/Larry_Hryb" title="Larry Hryb">Larry Hryb</a> (an employee at Microsoft and former radio broadcaster for <a href="/wiki/Clear_Channel_Communications" title="Clear Channel Communications">Clear Channel Communications</a>) and <a href="/wiki/Steve_Kroft" title="Steve Kroft">Steve Kroft</a> of <a href="/w/index.php?title=CBS_Sixty_Minutes&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="CBS Sixty Minutes (page does not exist)">CBS Sixty Minutes</a>.</p> 
     <p>Notable SU alumni in the performing arts include <a href="/wiki/Dick_Clark" title="Dick Clark">Dick Clark</a>, <a href="/wiki/Taye_Diggs" title="Taye Diggs">Taye Diggs</a>, <a href="/wiki/Peter_Falk" title="Peter Falk">Peter Falk</a>, <a href="/wiki/Frank_Langella" title="Frank Langella">Frank Langella</a>, <a href="/wiki/Aaron_Sorkin" title="Aaron Sorkin">Aaron Sorkin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rob_Edwards_(screenwriter)" title="Rob Edwards (screenwriter)">Rob Edwards</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jerry_Stiller" title="Jerry Stiller">Jerry Stiller</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Vanessa_L._Williams" title="Vanessa L. Williams">Vanessa L. Williams</a>.</p> 
     <p>Prominent athletes include the first African-American Heisman Trophy winner <a href="/wiki/Ernie_Davis" title="Ernie Davis">Ernie Davis</a>, immortalized in the motion picture &quot;<a href="/wiki/The_Express" title="The Express">The Express</a>&quot;;<a href="/wiki/Donovan_McNabb" title="Donovan McNabb">Donovan McNabb</a>, former quarterback in the <a href="/wiki/NFL" title="NFL" class="mw-redirect">NFL</a>; <a href="/wiki/Dwight_Freeney" title="Dwight Freeney">Dwight Freeney</a>, <a href="/wiki/Defensive_end" title="Defensive end">defensive end</a> for the <a href="/wiki/Indianapolis_Colts" title="Indianapolis Colts">Indianapolis Colts</a>; <a href="/wiki/Carmelo_Anthony" title="Carmelo Anthony">Carmelo Anthony</a>, forward for the <a href="/wiki/New_York_Knicks" title="New York Knicks">New York Knicks</a>; 7-time NBA All Star, pro basketball Hall of Famer and current Mayor of <a href="/wiki/Detroit" title="Detroit">Detroit</a> <a href="/wiki/Dave_Bing" title="Dave Bing">Dave Bing</a>; <a href="/wiki/Tim_Green" title="Tim Green">Tim Green</a>, who played football for the <a href="/wiki/Atlanta_Falcons" title="Atlanta Falcons">Atlanta Falcons</a> and a commentator for <a href="/wiki/National_Public_Radio" title="National Public Radio" class="mw-redirect">National Public Radio</a>; <a href="/wiki/Darryl_Johnston" title="Darryl Johnston" class="mw-redirect">Darryl Johnston</a>, who won three <a href="/wiki/Super_Bowl" title="Super Bowl">Super Bowl</a> rings with the <a href="/wiki/Dallas_Cowboys" title="Dallas Cowboys">Dallas Cowboys</a> in the 1990s; <a href="/wiki/Mikey_Powell" title="Mikey Powell" class="mw-redirect">Mikey Powell</a>, who plays lacrosse for the <a href="/wiki/Boston_Cannons" title="Boston Cannons">Boston Cannons</a>; <a href="/wiki/Jim_Brown" title="Jim Brown">Jim Brown</a>, NFL Hall of Famer and actor who had a long football career with the <a href="/wiki/Cleveland_Browns" title="Cleveland Browns">Cleveland Browns</a>; <a href="/wiki/Floyd_Little" title="Floyd Little">Floyd Little</a>, who played for the <a href="/wiki/Denver_Broncos" title="Denver Broncos">Denver Broncos</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Kyle_Johnson_(American_football)" title="Kyle Johnson (American football)">Kyle Johnson</a>, who played the majority of his NFL career with the <a href="/wiki/Denver_Broncos" title="Denver Broncos">Denver Broncos</a>; <a href="/wiki/John_Mackey_(American_football)" title="John Mackey (American football)">John Mackey</a> a member of the NFL Hall of Fame played for the legendary <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Baltimore_Colts" title="History of the Baltimore Colts">Baltimore Colts</a> (1963 -1971).</p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Affiliations">Affiliations</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Syracuse_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Affiliations">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Affiliated_Institutions">Affiliated Institutions</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Syracuse_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Affiliated Institutions">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="State_University_of_New_York_College_of_Environmental_Science_and_Forestry">State University of New York College of Environmental Science and Forestry</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Syracuse_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: State University of New York College of Environmental Science and Forestry">edit</a>]</span></h4> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/State_University_of_New_York_College_of_Environmental_Science_and_Forestry" title="State University of New York College of Environmental Science and Forestry">State University of New York College of Environmental Science and Forestry</a>
     </div> 
     <p>The College of Environmental Science and Forestry (ESF) has a long affiliation with Syracuse University, shares many campus resources, and operates its main academic campus immediately adjacent to Syracuse University. ESF was founded in 1911 as the <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_New_York_State_College_of_Forestry" title="History of the New York State College of Forestry">New York State College of Forestry</a> at Syracuse University, under the leadership of Syracuse University Trustee <a href="/wiki/Louis_Marshall" title="Louis Marshall">Louis Marshall</a>, with the active support of Syracuse University Chancellor Day. Its founding followed the Governor's veto of annual appropriations to a separate <a href="/wiki/New_York_State_College_of_Forestry_at_Cornell" title="New York State College of Forestry at Cornell">New York State College of Forestry at Cornell</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-agriculture_100-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-agriculture-100"><span>[</span>100<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>ESF is an autonomous institution, administratively separate from SU, while resources, facilities, and some infrastructure are shared. The two schools share a common Schedule of Classes; students at both institutions may take courses at the other, and degrees from ESF bear the Syracuse University seal along with the State University of New York. A number of concurrent degree programs and certificates are offered between the schools, as well. The college receives an annual appropriation as part of the SUNY budget and the state builds and maintains all of the college's educational facilities. The state has similar relationships with five <a href="/wiki/Statutory_college" title="Statutory college">statutory colleges</a> that are at <a href="/wiki/Alfred_University" title="Alfred University">Alfred University</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cornell_University" title="Cornell University">Cornell University</a>.</p> 
     <p>ESF faculty, students, and students' families join those from SU to take part in a joint convocation ceremony at the beginning of the academic year in August, and joint commencement exercises in May. ESF and SU students share access to libraries, recreational facilities, student clubs, and other activities at both institutions, except for the schools' intercollegiate sports teams, affiliated with the NCAA and NAIA, respectively. First-year ESF students live in the newly constructed Centennial Hall located on ESF's main campus.<sup id="cite_ref-The_ESF-SU_Relationship_101-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_ESF-SU_Relationship-101"><span>[</span>101<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="State_University_of_New_York_Upstate_Medical_University">State University of New York Upstate Medical University</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Syracuse_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: State University of New York Upstate Medical University">edit</a>]</span></h4> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/State_University_of_New_York_Upstate_Medical_University" title="State University of New York Upstate Medical University">State University of New York Upstate Medical University</a>
     </div> 
     <p>The medical school was formerly a college within SU, known as the Syracuse University Medical School. In 1950, SU sold the medical school to the <a href="/wiki/State_University_of_New_York" title="State University of New York">State University of New York</a> system. Beginning in the fall of 2009, a <a href="/wiki/Master_of_Public_Health" title="Master of Public Health" class="mw-redirect">Master of Public Health</a> degree program is now being offered by the two institutions. The program is the first of its kind in Central New York, and the first jointly offered by the two universities.<sup id="cite_ref-SUNY_Upstate_Medical_University.2C_Syracuse_University_Offer_Joint_Master_of_Public_Health_Degree_in_Fall_2009_102-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SUNY_Upstate_Medical_University.2C_Syracuse_University_Offer_Joint_Master_of_Public_Health_Degree_in_Fall_2009-102"><span>[</span>102<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Sejong-Syracuse_Global_MBA">Sejong-Syracuse Global MBA</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Syracuse_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Sejong-Syracuse Global MBA">edit</a>]</span></h4> 
     <p>The Sejong-Syracuse Global MBA program in Seoul, South Korea, was established by a joint effort between <a href="/wiki/Sejong_University" title="Sejong University">Sejong University</a> of Korea and Syracuse University in March 2001. Classes are taught by Syracuse and Sejong University professors as the first joint program establishing SU's presence in Asia.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Formerly_Affiliated_Institutions">Formerly Affiliated Institutions</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Syracuse_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Formerly Affiliated Institutions">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="State_University_of_New_York_at_Binghamton">State University of New York at Binghamton</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Syracuse_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: State University of New York at Binghamton">edit</a>]</span></h4> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/State_University_of_New_York_at_Binghamton" title="State University of New York at Binghamton" class="mw-redirect">State University of New York at Binghamton</a>
     </div> 
     <p>Binghamton was established in 1946 as Triple Cities College to serve the needs of local veterans returning from World War II of the Triple Cities area. Established in Endicott, New York, the college was a branch of Syracuse University. Triple Cities College offered local students the first two years of their education, while the following two were spent at Syracuse University. In 1946, students could earn their degrees entirely at the Binghamton campus. In 1950, it was absorbed by SUNY and renamed Harpur College.<sup id="cite_ref-About:_History_103-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-About:_History-103"><span>[</span>103<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Utica_College">Utica College</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Syracuse_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Utica College">edit</a>]</span></h4> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/Utica_College" title="Utica College">Utica College</a>
     </div> 
     <p><a href="/wiki/Utica_College" title="Utica College">Utica College</a>, an independent private university located in <a href="/wiki/Utica,_NY" title="Utica, NY" class="mw-redirect">Utica, NY</a>, was founded by Syracuse University in 1946. Utica College became independent from SU in 1995, but still offers its students the option to receive a specialized bachelor's degree from Syracuse University through a mutual relationship between the two schools.<sup id="cite_ref-Fast_Facts_104-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fast_Facts-104"><span>[</span>104<span>]</span></a></sup></p>

Syracuse University. 14 May 2011<span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved 16 December 2011</span>. &quot;Three Trustees shall be elected by the Board to represent the North Central New York, Western New York and Wyoming Conferences of the United Methodist Church. The Syracuse University Board of Trustees and the named conferences may recommend persons for election as Trustees in this capacity. The representatives need not reside in the areas they represent.&quot;</span><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ASyracuse+University&amp;rft.btitle=Syracuse+University+Bylaws%2C+Scope%3A+Trustees%2FUniversity+Governance&amp;rft.date=14+May+2011&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fsupolicies.syr.edu%2Fethics%2Fbylaws.htm&amp;rft.pub=Syracuse+University&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook" class="Z3988"><span style="display:none;">&nbsp;</span></span></span></li> 
       <li id="cite_note-Relatedness-14"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-Relatedness_14-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><span class="citation book"><i>A Brief Report of Church Relatedness: Syracuse University&nbsp;– INCORPORATION AND THE METHODIST CHURCH</i>. Syracuse University. 15 June 2010. &quot;The current bylaws authorize the Board to elect three Organization Trustees: one Trustee each to represent the North Central New York, Western New York, and Wyoming conferences of the United Methodist Church. Both the conferences and the Board may recommend persons for election as Organization Trustees. Today Syracuse University is considered a Methodist-related institution. Syracuse University's affiliation is expressed in the tradition, though not regulation, of having a United Methodist minister serve as dean of Hendricks Chapel and in the University's participation in the annual University Teacher/Scholar Award sponsored by the Methodist Church. In addition, the University administers a number of Methodist-funded scholarships and houses the Bishop Ledden Endowed Professorship in the Department of Religion.&quot;</span><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ASyracuse+University&amp;rft.btitle=A+Brief+Report+of+Church+Relatedness%3A+Syracuse+University%26nbsp%3B%E2%80%93+INCORPORATION+AND+THE+METHODIST+CHURCH&amp;rft.date=15+June+2010&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.pub=Syracuse+University&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook" class="Z3988"><span style="display:none;">&nbsp;</span></span> <span style="display:none;font-size:100%" class="error citation-comment"><code>|accessdate=</code> requires <code>|url=</code> (<a href="/wiki/Help:CS1_errors#accessdate_missing_url" title="Help:CS1 errors">help</a>)</span></span></li> 
       <li id="cite_note-William_Joseph_Whalen.C2.A0.E2.80.94_Hospitals_.26_Universities-15"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-William_Joseph_Whalen.C2.A0.E2.80.94_Hospitals_.26_Universities_15-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><span class="citation book"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://books.google.com/books?id=sw9ILcqw2hsC&amp;pg=PA162&amp;lpg=PA162&amp;dq=salvation+of+separated+brethren&amp;source=bl&amp;ots=ydrVxGCZ6w&amp;sig=L_-DZRvpoMtZSDkrT6HNQcmd4aU&amp;hl=en&amp;ei=xfSvS52yE4faNZX_zJkF&amp;sa=X&amp;oi=book_result&amp;ct=result&amp;resnum=3&amp;ved=0CA0Q6AEwAjgK#v=onepage&amp;q=methodist&amp;f=false"><i>Separated brethren: a review of Protestant, Anglican, Eastern Orthodox &amp; other religions in the United States</i></a>. <a href="/wiki/Our_Sunday_Visitor" title="Our Sunday Visitor">Our Sunday Visitor</a><span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved 2010-03-27</span>. &quot;Among Protestant denominations, Methodists take first place in hospitals and colleges. Some of their one hundred colleges and universities have all but severed ties with the denominations, but others remain definitely Methodist: Syracuse, Boston, Emory, Duke, Drew, Denver, and Southern Methodist. The church operates three hundred sixty schools and institutions overseas. Methodists established Goodwill Industries in 1907 to help handicapped persons help themselves by repairing and selling old furniture and clothes. The United Methodist Church runs seventy-two hospitals in the United States.&quot;</span><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ASyracuse+University&amp;rft.btitle=Separated+brethren%3A+a+review+of+Protestant%2C+Anglican%2C+Eastern+Orthodox+%26+other+religions+in+the+United+States&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fbooks.google.com%2Fbooks%3Fid%3Dsw9ILcqw2hsC%26pg%3DPA162%26lpg%3DPA162%26dq%3Dsalvation%2Bof%2Bseparated%2Bbrethren%26source%3Dbl%26ots%3DydrVxGCZ6w%26sig%3DL_-DZRvpoMtZSDkrT6HNQcmd4aU%26hl%3Den%26ei%3DxfSvS52yE4faNZX_zJkF%26sa%3DX%26oi%3Dbook_result%26ct%3Dresult%26resnum%3D3%26ved%3D0CA0Q6AEwAjgK%23v%3Donepage%26q%3Dmethodist%26f%3Dfalse&amp;rft.pub=Our+Sunday+Visitor&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook" class="Z3988"><span style="display:none;">&nbsp;</span></span></span></li>

       <li id="cite_note-A_Tragic_End_to_the_Semester-36"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-A_Tragic_End_to_the_Semester_36-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><span class="citation news">Yen, Marianne (December 23, 1988). &quot;A Tragic End to the Semester&quot;. <i>The Washington Post</i>. p.&nbsp;A07. &quot;Eggers was criticized for allowing a basketball game against Western Michigan to be played here Wednesday night.
